It&#x27;s super runny and does NOT thicken like hair dye. Just thought I&#x27;d warn you.</li>

    <li> One thing that I didn&#x27;t know until I had bought and opened the product, &amp;#34;Color Oops is not designed for and will not perform on direct color dyes such as bright pinks, blues, greens, lavendars, purples, etc.&amp;#34; I had red in my hair, and it turned it into a dark purple color. I was hoping that it would just take the red out and leave me with my weird orangy-bleached hair color so I could re-color it. I had to go to the salon to get it fixed. Here are my before and after pictures.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been coloring my hair dark reddish brownish black for many years, and it&#x27;s always been lighter and brighter on top than at the middle and bottom--which I hated! It had been about 5 weeks since my last at-home coloring, and I was tired of the uneven results so I wanted to try this product to attempt to get a more even result the next time I colored. My hair is VERY fine and can&#x27;t take the abuse of bleach, so honestly I was slightly terrified to try this. But I&#x27;m glad I did. Even though I have long hair, one box was enough. I started at the ends and went up to the roots. I wouldn&#x27;t say that it smelled good, but it was not nearly as strong as many other hair colors I&#x27;ve used. As it was processing I was nervous that it would get too light so I rinsed it out after 15 minutes instead of 20. (I probably should have done the strand test beforehand). I was surprised at how well it took the color out (I followed the rinsing and conditioning instructions). It was no where near my natural color (which is an ashy light brown) except at my roots which were unchanged, but I didn&#x27;t expect it return my hair to its natural color anyway. The result on my colored hair was a an orangey-blonde color; but it was still brighter on top of my head and probably 1-2 shades darker near the ends and underneath. I was a little disappointed that it didn&#x27;t turn out more even. But the next day it was a little less bright on top--thank goodness. I read another review that said she let the mixture process on her ends for 10 minutes before applying to the rest of her hair and now I wish I would have done that.</li>
    <li> I have used this product 3 or 4 times in the past few years, and it works fantastically. It removes the darkest colors, right down to the tips of my hair which have several layers of different hair color accumulated on them. Does it smell? YES. The smell is pretty awful, and this last time was the worst. I don&#x27;t know if they changed the formula slightly or if it was just me, but it hung around for a few days, despite repeated washing. So yeah, be prepared for that. Also, if you&#x27;ve used any hair color that had any lightening agents in it at all, you will end up with a brassy tone after the color is removed. The product removes all artificial color, but it cannot redeposit color that has been previously bleached out. Even if you&#x27;ve only tried to go a shade lighter or redder, you will have this issue. Be prepared to re-color with an ash-toned or &amp;#34;cool&amp;#34; color. Also, if you&#x27;re going to recolor your hair within a few days of using Color Oops, use a shade at least 2 shades lighter than what you want the result to be. The shaft of your  hair will be wide open and will suck up color like a sponge. This past time I wanted a light medium brown, so I colored my hair with a box of dark ash blonde. The directions also say to use a deep conditioner after using Color Oops, and I would second that. While my hair wasn&#x27;t wrecked, it was markedly drier.&lt;br /&gt;All in all, it&#x27;s a great product. I would highly recommend it to anyone wanting to fix a coloring mistake.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used 2 boxes one at night and one the next morning. My hair is now a brassy orange/red. It looks terrible &amp; was isn&#x27;t anywhere near where I wanted it. I followed everyones tips and read all the reviews. I am very frustrated. DON&#x27;T WASTE YOUR TIME OR MONEY!</li>
    <li> Purchased this product out of desperation a week after a bad dye job.  I was hesitant to put anything else on my hair, fearing more damage, but couldn&#x27;t have been more pleased by the results.  The process is a little time consuming, but WELL worth it!!  Not only did all the dye dissolve from my hair, but my hair was not damaged at all.  Beware: the smell is a bit strong, like that of a perm, but it does go away after shampooing.  Be sure to use a good conditioner afterwards.  I used Nutrogena Triple Action conditioner, left it on my hair for 5 minutes.  My hair is shiny, feels soft, and looks really healthy.  THANK YOU to whomever created this miracle dye-removing product!!!!!!!!</li>
    <li> I love this stuff. I was extremely skeptical at first, but decided I had nothing to lose. I dyed my hair Manic Panic&#x27;s Atomic Turquoise a week ago and got sick of the color really quickly. I bought some Color Oops, but when I got home and read the directions it clearly says it will not work on bright pinks, blues, greens or purples, but I did a test strip and it worked! And quickly too. It smells, but not as bad as bleach. It&#x27;s very easy to use. It didn&#x27;t itch or irritate my scalp and there was no visible damage. I don&#x27;t know how they do it, but this stuff is amazing. Highly recommended.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve now used this product a few times, and have learned:    1.  When they say rinse, RINSE!  The package says it will undo hair color in 20 minutes, but that&#x27;s just the application time.  You&#x27;ll easily spend another half hour or more just rinsing your hair.  The rinsing is very, very important, as it removes the old hair dye molecules from the hair shaft.  If you don&#x27;t rinse enough, those molecules will stay on your hair, waiting to re-oxidize (and there are lots of things out there, not just peroxide, that will \\&quot;oxidize\\&quot; those molecules, turning your hair dark).  So RINSE...until you think your arms are going to fall off.    2.  You&#x27;ll need to seal the hair shaft afterwards, some how, some way.  There will be some stubborn old dye molecules still stuck to your hair (especially if you didn&#x27;t rinse as much as necessary), and you do not want to reactivate them, or your hair will return to the color you were trying to get rid of.  So, you&#x27;ll want to create some sort of barrier between those old molecules and anything that can possibly oxidize them.  That means lots of protein products, and lots and lots of conditioning.</li>
    <li> I was soooo excited to take the color out of my hair, I&#x27;ve had it since October, and it is now December. Color Oops says it will take it out if it is a day, or a year old, so that shouldn&#x27;t matter anyway.     I googled ways to get rid of the color, vinegar, crappy shampoo, and Color Oops were all recommended. Color Oops had AMAZING reviews, and those that seemed bad, seemed like it was the users fault. I waited two weeks before finally being brave enough to go and get some, but I couldn&#x27;t find it at Sally&#x27;s, WalMart, Target, etc. I finally found some at Walgreens, and I bought two boxes (thick, long hair) I applied it, did EVERYTHING the box said to, I washed it really good because everyone seemingly said that that part was very, very important.     Nothing.    I&#x27;m now out $26, with my hair untouched. ABSOLUTELY UNTOUCHED. It didn&#x27;t do a THING to it. I&#x27;m absolutely disappointed. I&#x27;ve contacted DeveloPlus explaining my situation, I will follow up IF they reply.    I envy those of you who this worked for :/ I wish I had that luck.</li>
    <li> my hair was dyed dark brown and I wanted to use this to lift it a couple shades closer to my natural color (dark blonde) so I could color it again. I followed the instructions (lots of waiting and rinsing) and ended up with...dark brown. At most about 1/2 a shade lighter. The only thing I got out of this was a stinky bathroom and hair that felt like yarn. I definitely do not recommend using this, I&#x27;ve tried other color removers that work a lot better. Maybe if your hair is not a super dark shade it would lighten better but overall a giant waste of time and money.</li>
    <li> Everyone keeps talking about the rinse rinse rinsing. Well, why don&#x27;t you just use some of the shampoo&#x27;s that stop and get all the molecules out of the hair in the shampoo.     <li> Color Oops took my hair from a horrid purple burgundy to a light copper red (I&#x27;m blonde naturally). It is now much better as I am now blonde with coppery low lights.&lt;br /&gt;Yes, the stuff stinks, but it also works to get rid of very dark frightening hair dye. I washed 4 times and rinsed, while scrubbing very hard, the full 5 minutes each time.  Also, this product will not correct a bad lightening nor will it work on the new fangled colors which are not used with a lifter originally, lifter being a peroxide.  It has to be oxidized coloring.&lt;br /&gt;I am very pleased with this product and now know that I cannot have any salon do anything to my hair from here on out.  Thank you Clairol!</li>
    <li> My hair is naturally a dark brown, I have dyed it many times and more recently I dyed it a much lighter redish light brown. Then, wanting my old color back, I used garnier natural dark brown which turned my hair a hideous jet black. I came across this product and used it the next day. The smell isn&#x27;t even that bad and it worked great! My hair is now restored the the red light brown it was before. Great product.</li>
    <li> I used the new John Frieda foam hair color in a lovely light brown shade, my natural color.  I needed to color my grays. Well, to my utter shock &amp; disbelief, the color turned my hair dark, dark brown which looked plum in the sunlight.  I was horrified. I have never, ever worn my hair this dark in my life.  So, I remembered seeing a coupon for Color Oops and found some at the local retailer.  I bought the &#x27;extra strength&#x27; version as that is all they carried.      First, if you buy this product, be prepared as it has tons of directions and hints.  It takes time to sort through them and you&#x27;ll likely want to read them several times before you even consider beginning.  When I mixed the two chemicals together, I immediately thought it smelled like a home perm.  It&#x27;s stinky, but in a milder way.  It stinks, but it worked.  Probably the worst part about this product is the rinsing. But, do it.  It works.  When I was done, my hair was back to its normal color AND my grays were still covered.  I did have really bad split ends though, which I admit I had before I used this product, but it definitely made them worse and much more noticable.  And, that perm smell was still around two days later.  Thankfully, I had an appointment for a haircut a few days later &amp; the split ends are gone now.  I&#x27;m going to be using a heavy conditioner for at least the next few weeks to restore the moisture back to my hair. But, if I had it to do all over again, I would still buy this product.  It truly works.</li>
    <li> okay so i purchased this at a local walgreens since it was easier, and i had blue dye in my very lightly bleached blonde hair and this helped to remove most of it. there is still a hint of a light blue-ish hue but i like it so i dont care.&lt;br /&gt;!!!!warning!!!! this stuff is rank smelling like my whole house smelled like rotten eggs for more than a day. so my suggestion is if you can get someone to help you put this on but outside and then dispose of the remaining contents to outside garbage, and until its ready to wash out just sit outside until you rinse it out. trust me it will help also be ready to spend a lot of time rinsing this out it takes more then one shampoo-ing to get the smell off my hair. just wash your hair with a couple different shampoo&#x27;s if you can and it should help get rid of the smell.&lt;br /&gt;also make sure you use a conditioner so your hair doesn&#x27;t get too dry. good luck</li>
    <li> I used this product 2 weeks ago, and I absolutely recommend it.    I have brown hair with some gray, and I dyed my hair too dark - it was supposed to be dark brown, but it came out black. I waited a month for it to fade, but it didn&#x27;t. Finally, I tried Color Oops, and it worked perfectly.     I followed the directions exactly and even tacked on an extra 5 full minutes of rinsing. My hair was kind of an ashy blond color (lighter than natural color) for about 12 hours, but then it darkened to brown - exactly my natural shade.    My hair was dry for a day or two, but not bad. And I can still smell the terrible Color Oops smell a little bit sometimes (like, when I am washing my hair). But I would absolutely recommend this 100%.</li>
    <li> This product removed the excess color from the ends of my hair, but the sulphur smell lingered even after washing several times. To get rid of the rotten egg smell I opened up 10 vitamin C capsules and combined the powder with shampoo to create a paste and then washed my hair with it. After washing I rinsed my hair with hot water really well BEFORE using conditioner. I think it&#x27;s really important to rinse well before using conditioner which seals the cuticle of the hair. Hope this helps those who are sick of the awful smell.</li>

I actually felt like I was going to pass out (kinda scary) from the heat and smell together and 20 minutes is a long time. Radio helps.    After all of that I applied Original Hair Mayonnaise Conditioner and sat for 20 minutes with it on my hair. Then rinsed some more.     When I towel dried hair I noticed almost all color was removed, roots were brassy/light blonde and ends were dark blonde/light brunette.  I was happy it was almost back to normal. I proceeded to purchase two boxes of Color Oops, two boxes of hair color (Nice n Easy - Natural Dark Neutral Blonde and Natural Lightest Golden Brown) in case I had an \\&quot;omg\\&quot; moment, a shower cap, a wide-toothed comb and a thermal conditioning treatment (heavy duty conditioner). If you use Color Oops, I highly recommend making sure you have all these items handy. Also, read the box insert, and know it like the back of your hand. This is a must.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Make sure to do a strand test. Cut out a small piece of your hair and just do it, or you&#x27;ll be sorry later. Check it every five minutes so you can see the various shades of change and decide on the best time for your hair. They recommend no longer than 20 minutes. Based on mine, I saw my hair change from red to blonde after 20 minutes and elected to leave it on for the full amount of time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE PROCESS&lt;br /&gt;Still, I was super nervous as I prepared the mixture and dumped it on my hair. It is a thin mixture, maybe a bit thicker than water but not by much, so be careful with the dribbles. I didn&#x27;t notice any bleaching effect on the red robe I was wearing. As everyone else has said, it has a very strong odor - citrus and sulfur, so be prepared. I made sure to spread the mixture quickly and evenly, using the wide-toothed comb to ensure that my hair was fully saturated, then put the shower cap on to help \\&quot;lock\\&quot; in the product. I avoided being in cool areas of my house, as the insert said this could cause it not to process correctly (also a good reason to use the shower cap). I&#x27;d recommend checking your hair periodically, even after the strand test, so you don&#x27;t let it go too long.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Rinsing it out was a breeze in the shower. This is the most important part of the process. I kept the water warm, rinsed for several minutes, shampooed and rinsed for several minutes, and repeated once more. Rinse until your water gets cold, no joke! Your hair may feel a little stiff at this point, so use your restoring conditioner after the second shampoo. I had some left over from an older Nice n Easy kit and it worked better than the thermal treatment I bought specifically for this purpose (read on to find out why I ended up having to condition twice).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE MOMENT OF TRUTH&lt;br /&gt;After I got out of the shower I could tell right away that my hair was looking pretty bleached blonde and much lighter than my natural color, but probably due to the previous dyeing I&#x27;d done (most over-the-counter permanent dyes include a bleaching agent, no matter what color you choose). I dried it using my blow dryer and it came out looking pale and brassy - almost a strawberry blonde. My boyfriend said, \\&quot;Your hair is kind of orange...\\&quot; I didn&#x27;t think it was hideous, but not exactly what I had envisioned. It didn&#x27;t seem damaged, either, though I had very healthy hair to start with.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;REDYEING AFTER COLOR OOPS&lt;br /&gt;So I started thinking about that boxof blonde hair color I bought to use after the Color Oops, in case it didn&#x27;t turn out. Color Oops recommends using a color filler if you choose to dye right after the color removal process. They also advise that you choose a lighter, warmer shade than that of what you are trying to achieve and say not to let it process for more than several minutes. I skipped the color filler and applied just the color, noticing that by the time I&#x27;d applied it to my whole head, it had already \\&quot;taken\\&quot; and rushed to rinse it out, but it was too late. After no more than just a few minutes, the blonde hair color had turned my hair a distinct brown, and on the ashy side (even though it was labeled a \\&quot;neutral\\&quot; shade). That wasn&#x27;t the hair color&#x27;s fault, though - it was mine. The box insert is not joking. Use a color filler and/or buy at least a couple shades warmer and lighter than your desired end result if you are dyeing right after Color Oops. So if you&#x27;re looking to go medium/dark blonde, buy a golden light blonde (or even lightest blonde).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;COLOR OOPS... TAKE TWO!&lt;br /&gt;Luckily, I had bought the second box of Color Oops, did another strand test, and decided to leave it in for only 15 minutes this time. I got the same result as the first Oops application (glowing blonde hair), and still little, if any, damage. Stinky, though. I don&#x27;t notice the smell one day after, if that&#x27;s any consolation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE AFTER GLOW&lt;br /&gt;Realize that the rinsing process is absolutely the most important part of making Color Oops work (yes, I&#x27;m reiterating, but honestly it can&#x27;t be repeated enough). Even after what I thought was excessive rinsing, I did notice that my color darkened overnight, meaning that the first application probably would have done the same thing if I&#x27;d been patient. I am still blonde, but not back to my natural caramel blonde. It appears very golden with some glowing reddish tones, which could be from the previous dyeing, but definitely toned down after just 8 hours. I have actually received compliments today on the new color, and told people that I had my hair stripped at the salon. They commented that it didn&#x27;t appear damaged at all. The results are that good. Just be aware that you will likely have some darkening up to 24 hours after you complete the process (and also take this into account if you are redyeing).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE END?&lt;br /&gt;Sorry this was so long. I learned quite a bit about Color Oops by reading reviews and realize that this information is invaluable to other people who are thinking about taking the risk to get their hair back to normal (or at least close to it). I hope the detail in this review helps you to relax and embark on your Color Oops adventure!of blonde hair color I bought to use after the Color Oops, in case it didn&#x27;t turn out.     <li> I have a lot of thick hair that&#x27;s cut into a chin-length bob and I had been coloring it soft black for over 6 months to hide my grays and also blend in a bad color job that left sections of my hair a strange red color.  The soft black had been doing a great job but I just turned 43 and it&#x27;s summertime and I felt like it was too harsh for my age and time of the year so I read a lot of reviews and watched a lot of videos on YouTube and decided that for the price, Color Oops was the one I was going to try.    My hairdresser was afraid to use anything on my hair to take the black out and she suggested lightening it through session after session of weaving. I was never convinced that I was going to be satisfied with those results and I can truthfully say that for $12, I am happier with my results.    Let me just say that I have really strong hair that can take a real BEATING but that my scalp is on the sensitive side.  I did not do the sensitivity test or color test either....which I probably should have done but I was eager to get the black out.    I left the product on for 30 minutes instead of the recommended 20 BECAUSE my hair is strong and in good condition.  If your hair is not like mine, you probably should not leave it on that long.  I put the heat cap on and went out to my back yard in the sun because the directions say not to be anywhere in the cold or where cold air can hit your head.  The secret is in the heat while it&#x27;s processing AND in the amount of time you spend rinsing it out of your hair.      I came in and took a shower letting the water hit my head 30 minutes making sure it was all out and also shampooed with a dandruff shampoo one time and frizz control shampoo the second time.  I was hot and tired from the hot water by the time it was all done, but I&#x27;m happy I took that long rinsing because the results were totally worth it.  I also used deep conditioner that I had saved from a previous hair coloring to apply right after and also sat with my hair in a different heat cap for 20 minutes.  My hair was not damaged or dried out or fried in the least.    The black is completely gone from my hair.  It&#x27;s now a darkish brown with pleasant shades of red throughout.  I&#x27;ve never lightened my hair anytime so there are no traces of bleaching/lightening that other people might find with their hair.  The product takes all of the dark pigments out of your hair that have been deposited by coloring your hair.  It does not take any bleaching/lightening pigments out of your hair because that&#x27;s not what it&#x27;s designed to do.    The directions say you can color your hair the same day, but if you don&#x27;t seal your hair with a conditioner after using Oops, then your hair is going to be VERY VERY porous and will grab the hair color like a sponge.  If you have to color your hair again immediately, be sure to use the deep conditioner FIRST so your hair will not soak up the color as much.  If you can wait several days in between using this product and coloring your hair, that&#x27;s even better because your hair will become less porous over time.  Also, be certain that you choose a hair color that is LIGHTER than the shade you are trying to become.  Everyone who has used this and the company all say that if you use a dark shade to color your hair that you&#x27;re going to be back in the same boat that brought you here in the first place.  So IF you must recolor, go lighter.    The only down-side to Color Oops is that it does smell like sulfur or rotten eggs to some extent because of the chemicals used.  But there is NO bleach or ammonia!  If you can open a window wherever you&#x27;re applying the product, do so and be sure you have a garbage sack to throw the bottles and heat cap away after you&#x27;re finished and that will help air your house out faster.  Also, if you have a strongly scented conditioner or leave-in treatment to put on your hair afterward, that will also help get the smell out of your own hair.  It&#x27;s really NOT that bad.  I asked 3 differentpeople to smell my hair after I was all done and none of them told me that I stunk.  I promise, it&#x27;s all okay!    Just follow the package directions and read as many other reviews and tips that you can.  It will remove the dark pigments from hair coloring just like it says.  And if it can work on my hair, it can certainly work on yours.</li>

    <li> Color Oops WILL remove too much or unwanted hair color. If your hair was colored before the latest \\&quot;oops\\&quot;, it will also remove that color, leaving you most likely with yellow-y, orange-y, and somewhat uneven hair that in most cases will require additional coloring to be transformed into something pretty;-) At this point you have two choices:  1) Immediately (possibly wearing a hat?) go to a professional salon, explain what happened, and let THEM do the job with demi-permanent color of your choice. I recommend to ask the stylist to treat your hair with a protein filler before coloring it, or better yet, do it at home right after \\&quot;color oops\\&quot;. This is a foolproof way of getting preferred hair color and saves you quite some money, since this isn&#x27;t a \\&quot;correction\\&quot; anymore, but a single process dye job.  2) At home - If you are coloring your hair yourself, you HAVE to have a \\&quot;Neutral Protein Filler\\&quot; (sally&#x27;s, amazon). Use it as a leave-in conditioner BEFORE a hair dye job. The filler will restore the structure of your hair, so subsequently applied color will grab on evenly. The treatment also helps covering grey, avoid the \\&quot;hot root\\&quot; effect, and overly processed ends. I apply this treatment even before professional dye treatments. I am really, really pleased with the results! Less damage, better color, no oversaturation. For those going brunette: Use a NEUTRAL shade (to avoid too much red) of a medium/dark blond or light brown demi-permanent hair color or hair gloss. Put protein treatment in your hair, wait 20 min., don&#x27;t rinse!!! TIP for those fearing too much red - buy the \\&quot;UNRED\\&quot; drops (Ricky&#x27;s, Sally&#x27;s, Amazon). Add a few drops (following the instructions) to the color mix, this will take care of the unwanted red. After putting the color mix on your roots, massage it through the rest of your hair, let it sit for 5-10 min. max! This should be enough time for the color to grab. Rinse, wash, rinse, deeply condition, style. VoilÃ , your new color!  Other tip based on experience:  If your hair turned very light and you want to go to a deeper brown shade, you want to use a double process. First you color with a light strawberry blonde/light golden blonde, after that you color with a neutral shade of medium/dark blonde/light brunette. This will give your hair a nice dimension and add gloss. You probably will still end up on a \\&quot;warmer\\&quot; side.</li>

Anyway, the results: this product stripped my color back to the medium-dark brown I was accustomed to and I didn&#x27;t even need to recolor to correct anything (which I was prepared to do).  So, while it&#x27;s not going to strip you to natural if you&#x27;ve been coloring for a while, it will lighten up black dye to a reasonable, \\&quot;ok to leave the house again\\&quot; color! It became apparent there are so many people online, RIGHT NOW, looking up ways to fix their overly dark awful dye job (some home, some from salons). The message boards are full of desperate, horrified people, of all ages and genders, trying to fix their hair. There are many &#x27;cures&#x27;, from the ridiculous (pouring diluted clorox bleach on hair) to helpful (wash w/drops of Dawn dish soap mixed with Prell shampoo, rinse with hottest poss. water, condition, repeat for a month). I don&#x27;t know why it took me four hours to find Color Oops, but it did, and by this time I was convinced there were no quick fixes, just tedious, somewhat useful fading techniques. That being said, however, C.O. seemed unusual enough that I began to wade through about 500 reviews on Walgreens.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  Following the instructions is EVERYTHING with this product (I know, right? Me? Following instructions to a T? But I&#x27;m an American! I have instruction rights!) Also, it only works with hair that has gone darker, not hair that has been lightened. Be prepared to spend some quality time counting tiles in your shower; the rinsing time is critically important. The infamous smell isn&#x27;t a problem, because, when you (or, say, your teen) have a wretched dye job and you are wailing \\&quot;I&#x27;ll do anything, ANYTHING to fix this, I can&#x27;t live with this!\\&quot;, a temporary sulfuric, rotten egg-type smell is a small price to pay. The smell doesn&#x27;t last past a day, anyway. You can always put a little perfume on to distract your nose (which fragrance notes work well with eau d&#x27;egg rot? There&#x27;s gotta be something). Also extremely important: the test strand. I cut about twenty hairs for a tiny but thick enough strand to observe results. I left the solution on for the instructed 20 min, and after rinsing, it seemed too light for her original hair color.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  For the actual process, I used a timer on my cell, which was more helpful to me than setting an alarm, because I knew precisely how much time had passed. We left the solution on for 13 minutes (I had intended to have her start rinsing at the 10 minute mark, considering how light the test strand went after 20 min, but it ended up being 13 minutes because I had a cooking interruption). She rinsed with warm, not hot, water because we didn&#x27;t want the heater to run out too quickly, shampooed for 5 minutes, rinsed for 20, shampooed again for 5, rinsed for 20, shampooed a third time, rinsed for ten, and then got out of the shower. The odor was mostly gone by this time, and in point of fact, the smell wasn&#x27;t as much an issue as the marathon rinsing. It really seemed endless. She had the radio on to help with the tedium, but it was a good thing we used the cell timer, as we both kept saying \\&quot;Oh surely it&#x27;s been time enough\\&quot;, and discovered to our chagrin that it wasn&#x27;t.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  I didn&#x27;t have her use conditioner, as I had a packet of olive oil/orange oil deep conditioning mask for her to sleep in, under a shower cap (I use it all the time, it&#x27;s lovely. $1.50 for single use packet at Walgreens). Her hair, even wet, looked almost exactly like it did back before she started ever dying it. I was amazed. I just couldn&#x27;t believe such a remarkable transformation. The next morning, she rinsed off the mask, used a tiny drop of BioSilk on the ends, and blew it out with the dryer. Her hair was BEAUTIFUL. It once again looks like milk chocolate with those reddish hues when the sun hits it.  A week and two shampoos later, it&#x27;s still beautiful. She has only been blowing out her bangs, the rest she lets dry overnight, just to baby the hair a bit. I&#x27;ve read reviews about successful color reversals, but with a lot of damage, to the point where they question if they should have just let the hair fade with other timely techniques. I don&#x27;t know if it&#x27;s because she has only been dying her hair for a few years, but it&#x27;s not terribly damaged. A little bit, yes, but not enough to merit concern. Almost certainly her hair would be more damaged if we had dyed again after the C.O. to achieve her desired shade, but we lucked out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  I love this product. If I had known of it when I was younger, I could have avoided a lot of my own hair drama. If possible, I&#x27;d like to implore the makers of C.O. to branch out: Marriage Oops, I Ate The Whole Box Of Fudge When My Period Started Oops, I Looked Away For Two Seconds To Snarl At My Kids And Nailed The Bumper Of The Mercedes In Front Of Me Whose Driver Turned Out To Be A Lawyer Oops. She rinsed with warm, not hot, water because we didn&#x27;t want the heater to run out too quickly, shampooed for 5 minutes, rinsed for 20, shampooed again for 5, rinsed for 20, shampooed a third time, rinsed for ten, and then got out of the shower. The odor was mostly gone by this time, and in point of fact, the smell wasn&#x27;t as much an issue as the marathon rinsing. It really seemed endless. Was dark auburn at the time of using product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I decided to go back to blonde because it was too much hassle keeping up with the roots, its a normal thing that happens with me every few years, but I didn&#x27;t want to wait for my hair to grow out so I did some research and found Color Oops.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have short, shoulder length, thick hair. I needed two boxes to fully saturate my hair. I probably could have used three but two did the job. Since my hair is so thick I let it set for about 40 minutes. If you have thick hair you need to or it won&#x27;t do anything. My friend has much thinner hair and after fifteen minutes her hair was starting to lighten, just as a comparison.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The application doesn&#x27;t smell so bad but after you&#x27;ve washed it out there will be a lingering sulfur smell for a few days, its easily covered with another application of conditioner. The hair will feel a little dry at first, especially if you use heat on your hair so be wary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;YOU MUST RINSE FOR TWENTY MINUTES. With the hottest water you can take. Then wash for 5 minutes. Rise for 5 minutes. And repeat 4 more times. Use a shampoo that moisturizes so your hair doesn&#x27;t become like straw.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It will get super light and then darken. You can dye if you want right after but if you let it settle for a few days it won&#x27;t interfere with the dying process as much. It didn&#x27;t take my hair back to my natural color, but it got close and left it with a strawberry blonde shade and I&#x27;m still deciding if I want to dye it lighter but was a much easier and cheaper process than doing it at a salon. I suggest it to anyone that wants to go back to their natural color.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;FAIR WARNING: If you have ever bleached your hair, it will not come out so nicely it will be much more like an orange color, so you might want to look into dying it afterward.</li>
    <li> This product is wonderful! I have natural red hair - the kind that does not come in a bottle. If I had a dollar for every compliment I have received on my natural hair color, I would be rich. Too bad we are never satisfied. I have colored my hair many times over the years and as soon as I dye it, I am on a mission to get my natural hair color back - because nothing ever looks right. For years I have used bleach to correct my hair color mishaps. Of course that is damaging and always leaves my hair much lighter than I prefer. So anyhow this time I used color oops and if I am dumb enough to try to achieve a better color for myself again, I will know exactly what to use to fix my mistake. This is what happened this time. And yes, I know this will make me seem extremely idiotic. But maybe it will help you! I colored my hair a chocolate cherry mousse. It came out very artificial looking. Quite disgusting in my opinion. It had a deep pink tint that I just could not handle. The next day I went to the beauty supply and got a dark auburn color thinking this would make it more of a brown. Besides, auburn was more of what I was going for in the first place. It made it even darker, but still had that pink tint. I let it sit over the the weekend. I actually got compliments on it, but felt it did not look right with my skin color. So on Monday I tried the color oops. I did exactly what it said. And btw I was not gagging over the smell - and I am 6 months pregnant. (Yes - I got the ok from my DR.) The smell is bad, but completely tolerable. Once I started rinsing I saw that my hair looked normal. I was very excited. I rinsed and rinsed and rinsed until the water ran cold. I used a crappy shampoo hoping this would help to strip my hair. By the time I finished rinsing I  thought the color already looked like it had darkened back up. Boo. After I dried my hair it was lighter. Not normal, but lighter. It did look better. I was hoping it would take more out, but like I said, it was better. So a couple weeks past and the idiot strikes again. I had a box of hair color in the cabinet that was closer to my natural hair color. It showed that it would turn dark brown hair red. It didn&#x27;t. Maybe because my hair was artificially brown. So there I was with darker hair again. After smacking myself a few times for not just leaving it alone, I used the highlighting kit that came with the dye. The highlights came out great. And honestly if I had just skipped the last coloring and just highlighted my hair after the last color oops, I would have been happy... I think. So another couple of weeks go by and although my hair looks much better I was still annoyed with how dark it was underneath the highlights. So I started think I might try another color oops on it. That brings us to today. I was much faster about applying the color oops today - not sure why, but I guess I am getting good at it! And it does say to apply it quickly. I used a wide tooth comb and combed through it a couple times while applying. After the time was up I put a step ladder in the shower to sit on - because like I said I am pregnant. Standing in the shower for 30+ minutes is very uncomfortable these days. I rinsed for about 5 minutes and then used head and shoulders - since I read that dandruff and clarifying shampoos help remove color. Then I rinsed for 20 minutes and washed it again. Then I rinsed for 5 more. I do have very thick and long hair so I did not want to skimp on the rinsing. The entire time I rinsed I noticed that my hair looked normal. I kept waiting for it to darken back up. I got out of the shower and towel dried my hair. It looked much lighter than before. I applied a deep conditioner that said to leave it on for 5 minutes and rinse. I didn&#x27;t rinse though because my hair felt like crap. I then dried my hair with the conditioner on it. I still have not noticed it darkening and it feels soft and I look like me again. After about $80 of products I look nearly the same as I did before I started. Point being that if I had used Color Oops after the first coloring I could have saved myself a lot of time and money. Hopefully you will benefit from this. Oh and btw I picked this product up at Walgreen&#x27;s for $13.99.</li>
    <li> My hair is shoulder length - thick and coarse - naturally dark brown/black but that was years ago. I&#x27;ve been dying my hair dark brown/black for at least 10 years. Lately, I&#x27;ve been trying to find a way to allow my grey (80%ish) to grow in without the skunk look. I tried the spray color to avoid dying my roots (no good) and then switched to a semi-permanent to try and even out the color while it grew out...as directed by the experts I went a shade or two lighter to gradually step-down but what I ended up with was red roots with the warm brown and yellow roots with the natural brown...also no good. So, I decided that removing the color and then re-dying a lighter brown would be the best bet.  I headed to Wal-Mart and in anticipation of the amount of dye in my hair I grabbed two boxes of the OOPS ES.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as the product goes, it&#x27;s easy to use. Mix it just like hair dye, apply it to dry hair just like hair dye, cover and wait 20 min (just like hair dye), and rinse. It&#x27;s clear and really runny (unlike hair dye) so be prepared and wear something that you can ruin. I have a special turtle neck I use just for coloring my hair (helps keep it off my neck and arms). It has a sulfur smell but no one in the house complained. So, I did another application, same steps as above but I rinsed much longer since I know the hair darkening over time was due to color particles that were left behind and re-oxidized. This time my hair came out a beautiful and even strawberry dirty blonde from root to tip. I got lots of compliments on it all evening, it was really shiny and natural looking, I decided I wasn&#x27;t even going to color over it until the grow-out was noticeable. I put a light-weight overnight conditioner in my hair to help with any damage and went to bed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was really sad to wake-up and see that I was back to gold/brown roots and dark medium brown hair. Yeah, it blends in better with my eyebrows, but basically at almost $10 a box, my hair looks like it did before I started removing the color...$20 down the drain. It&#x27;s not worth trying another box at that price - especially since the whole purpose of the home treatment is because I couldn&#x27;t afford the professional treatment....and I&#x27;ve run the hot water out of the shower both time I applied the OOPS ES, so rinsing longer doesn&#x27;t seem to be the answer. Either the dye in my hair is too much or the OOPS is not enough.  I&#x27;m told that One and Only Color Fix by Conair is better, I will try that next but unless anyone else has any suggestions, if it doesn&#x27;t work I don&#x27;t know what else to do.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This might be a good product is you are removing a light color or if you are removing a single application of color. If you are a regular dark colored dye user you might want to test it but be prepared. Also, to put a few ideas to rest...there is not a single color remover or fixer that will return you to your natural color. All dyes leave a base - usually red, orange, or yellow, though sometimes blue/purple - that&#x27;s why I ended up with yellow, red, and strawberry blonde. If you don&#x27;t like the results (most won&#x27;t) - You will have to re-dye your hair after using the removers/fixers, just re-dye to a color a shade or two lighter than your natural color (or the desired color). Once you use a remover/fixer your hair is more porous and locks on to more color - so any color will turn out a shade or two darker than it is supposed to - use a shade or two lighter, you can always dye darker again if you need to...for most though, one dye to return you to your natural (or desired) color will be all you need.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It recommends that you use a protein filler before coloring to help reduce the amount of color your hair soaks up. Walmart sells them by single use packets in the hair care isle, usually next to the ethnic hair care....mine was less than $2...Sally&#x27;s Beauty Supply also sells them that way. I used one as a treatment to help reduce damage - I haven&#x27;t colored yet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If anyone else has any ideas I&#x27;d love to hear them - hope this review helps!</li>

    <li> This stuff works nearly as well as it claims to. I had medium brown hair with highlights and tried to dye it a dark brown, but it came out utterly black. All it does is remove the dye, it can&#x27;t restore colour to hair that was stripped with bleach or highlights, so don&#x27;t bother unless you accidentally dyed it too dark.&lt;br /&gt;-The smell is very strong and it will take days to rinse out.&lt;br /&gt;-Even though it isn&#x27;t bleach, it will dry out your hair so have some reparative conditioner to use after.&lt;br /&gt;-If you want to dye it again right after, you need to buy a lighter shade than normal. The hair will be porous and will soak up a huge amount of dye, meaning you will end up with too-dark hair all over again if you aren&#x27;t careful about getting a light enough colour.&lt;br /&gt;-The mixture is thin, my hair only goes to my chin and I still used the whole bottle. It&#x27;s important so don&#x27;t skip it! I chose this shade, which is a lot lighter than my intended color, because I kept reading that after the Color Oops, my hair would grab on to the color much more readily and turn it darker. Now, the Protein Filler was supposed to remedy this, but my hair always ends up much darker than the box so I thought that this would be a safe choice anyway. I reasoned that if the color really turned out too light, it is much easier to fix than if it turns out too dark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE PROCESS:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;STEP 1: Stripping Color&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I brushed through my hair and quickly mixed and applied the Color Oops through my head. The smell was pretty bad and my eyes burned as I was applying it. It was tolerable, though. The consistency of the product is NOT water as other reviews have said. I&#x27;d say it&#x27;s probably closer to the consistency of liquid hand soap. Once I was done applying it, I put the shower cap that came with the Color Oops on. The cap is actually pretty small... it won&#x27;t fit you if you have a lot of hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After 20 minutes, I returned to the bathroom. Upon inspection, my hair didn&#x27;t seem to have changed that much... it went from a faded light auburn to a milk chocolate brown, so I wasn&#x27;t sure what to expect. I set a kitchen timer to 30 minutes and put it by the shower so I could see it. Knowing the importance of the rinsing part of the process, I wanted to make sure that I spent enough time doing it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hopped into the shower and began rinsing. Once I&#x27;d gotten most of the product out, I applied my Seventh Generation dish soap and proceeded to wash my hair thoroughly. I rinsed it all out and repeated the process three times. When the timer was down to 5 minutes, Iapplied a good amount of L&#x27;Oreal Vitamino masque and let it sit for a few minutes while I proceeded to finish my shower as normal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I let my hair dry naturally and immediately noticed it was orange. Not pumpkin orange but more like tree leaves in the Fall kind of orange. Very much expected, since my hair had obviously been lightened by the repeated dying processes over the last few years. This meant that Color Oops had successfully done its job! However, I couldn&#x27;t keep this color.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, a lot of reviews say that Color Oops did not damage their hair, and frankly, I don&#x27;t know what they&#x27;re talking about. My hair felt very smooth and healthy in the beginning... but even with the masque I applied, my hair did NOT feel good after Color Oops. It wasn&#x27;t as bad as bleaching, but it definitely felt rough.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It was late, so I decided to go to bed and dye my hair in the morning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;STEP 2: Restoring your Color&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I started out by moistening my hair slightly and then combed through it and pretty much saturated it with the Neutral Protein filler. I could have applied it on dry hair, but that makes it more difficult to comb through. I let it sit for 20 minutes, which turned it to straw as it dried. This is normal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I proceeded to apply my dye right on top of the protein filler, Clairol Perfect 10 in Lightest Golden Brown (6.5G) and put on the shower cap included.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At this point, I knew that I was only supposed to leave the dye for 5 minutes, according to the Color Oops box. However, considering that I had applied a protein filler and the dye was a lot lighter than I intended, I decided to leave it the full 10 minutes that this particular brand requires. This turned out to be the correct decision! Read on...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once the 10 minutes were up, I hopped in the shower. I added a bit of water to my head and used the dye to make lather like shampoo, then rinsed out til water ran clear. I put on another healthy dose of L&#x27;Oreal Vitamino masque and again let it sit while I finished my shower.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Before stepping out, I rinsed out my hair with cold water. Mind you, I live in Upstate NY, so it is more like ice cold this time of the year. Good way to wake you up in the morning! It also helps close your hair cuticle and keep the color in ;) Don&#x27;t miss this step! Though you may want to just invert your head into the bathtub so you don&#x27;t freeze like I did.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE AFTERMATH:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Right after dying my hair, I let it airdry. At this point, I thought the color turned out a little too light and too brassy. It didn&#x27;t look bad at all, but it wasn&#x27;t what I wanted. So, I came back to Amazon and ordered a box of [[ASIN:B001LFEVSK Clairol Perfect 10 in Medium Ash Brown (5A)]]. I figured I&#x27;d throw it on for five minutes and that would darken the color and neutralize the brassiness. It was a good plan...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That was two days ago and I just received it. However, an interesting thing happened... My color seems to have \\&quot;settled\\&quot; and it now looks exactly the shade I wanted! I have not applied any shampoo yet, so this is most likely due to the previous Color Oops application. I have read this happened to other people. If you&#x27;re curious, look at the box model of [[ASIN:B0015NMSHY Clairol Perfect 10 in Medium Golden Brown (5G)]] and that&#x27;s exactly what my head looks like. It&#x27;s the actual shade I was shooting for, and it&#x27;s a tiny bit lighter than my natural color.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My hair actually feels really good after the dye application. It is very soft and shiny, though the ends still feel a little bit rough. Overall, I am happy with the final color and feel of my hair. I don&#x27;t plan to use the additional dye I purchased immediately, but I will keep it in case that it fades too much over the next few washes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will update this review if any further changes occur, but for now, consider me a happy customer!as normal.    I let my hair dry naturally and immediately noticed it was orange. Not pumpkin orange but more like tree leaves in the Fall kind of orange. Very much expected, since my hair had obviously been lightened by the repeated dying processes over the last few years. This meant that Color Oops had successfully done its job! However, I couldn&#x27;t keep this color.    Now, a lot of reviews say that Color Oops did not damage their hair, and frankly, I don&#x27;t know what they&#x27;re talking about. My hair felt very smooth and healthy in the beginning... but even with the masque I applied, my hair did NOT feel good after Color Oops. It wasn&#x27;t as bad as bleaching, but it definitely felt rough.    It was late, so I decided to go to bed and dye my hair in the morning.    STEP 2: Restoring your Color    I started out by moistening my hair slightly and then combed through it and pretty much saturated it with the Neutral Protein filler. I could have applied it on dry hair, but that makes it more difficult to comb through. I let it sit for 20 minutes, which turned it to straw as it dried. This is normal.    I proceeded to apply my dye right on top of the protein filler, Clairol Perfect 10 in Lightest Golden Brown (6.5G) and put on the shower cap included.    At this point, I knew that I was only supposed to leave the dye for 5 minutes, according to the Color Oops box. However, considering that I had applied a protein filler and the dye was a lot lighter than I intended, I decided to leave it the full 10 minutes that this particular brand requires. This turned out to be the correct decision! Read on...    Once the 10 minutes were up, I hopped in the shower. I added a bit of water to my head and used the dye to make lather like shampoo, then rinsed out til water ran clear. I put on another healthy dose of L&#x27;Oreal Vitamino masque and again let it sit while I finished my shower.    Before stepping out, I rinsed out my hair with cold water. Mind you, I live in Upstate NY, so it is morelike ice cold this time of the year. Good way to wake you up in the morning! It also helps close your hair cuticle and keep the color in ;) Don&#x27;t miss this step! Though you may want to just invert your head into the bathtub so you don&#x27;t freeze like I did.    THE AFTERMATH:    Right after dying my hair, I let it airdry. At this point, I thought the color turned out a little too light and too brassy. It didn&#x27;t look bad at all, but it wasn&#x27;t what I wanted. So, I came back to Amazon and ordered a box of [[ASIN:B001LFEVSK Clairol Perfect 10 in Medium Ash Brown (5A)]]. I figured I&#x27;d throw it on for five minutes and that would darken the color and neutralize the brassiness. It was a good plan...    That was two days ago and I just received it. However, an interesting thing happened... My color seems to have \\&quot;settled\\&quot; and it now looks exactly the shade I wanted! I have not applied any shampoo yet, so this is most likely due to the previous Color Oops application. I have read this happened to other people.     <li> Alright, so a little back story for ya, I&#x27;m 21 years old who has NEVER dyed her hair before. I decided, hey, time for a change! Let&#x27;s try ombre. Specifically light brown(natural color) to blonde at tips. This product had great reviews online, some bad some good, as you could probably tell because I&#x27;m probably one of 20 you just read. My hair is long (about mid way down my back) and thick so I prepared two bottles and i ended up used 100% of one bottle and 50% of the other. Definitely do a test strand first! I cut a chunk of hair off in the middle of my head on the one side(the least obvious place) and when i was finished with the test, I was very pleased with the color. On a side note, I just left the test strand in the sink. I didn&#x27;t put it in the sun or near a heater or anything. My house is probably 67-70 degrees right now. The only reason I&#x27;m sharing this is because it&#x27;s VERY important that you are extremely consistent. If you leave your test strand in the sink, just bend over and leave your hair in the tub for as long as you can stand it. You WILL get different results if your test strand is in the heat, washed for 2 minutes, shampoo, etc. and then when you treat your head, it&#x27;s cold water, rinse for 5 minutes, etc. so make sure if you do anything, it&#x27;s stay consistent so the results you see on the test strand is exactly what your whole head will look like. Make sure you time it too! It&#x27;s recommended for 20 minutes but everyone on the reviews seems to steer you away from that time. Personally, I figured I&#x27;d rather haveit in for not long enough than too long so I went with 10 minutes for the test strand and 8 minutes when I covered my entire head(left 2 minutes for application time so i stayed consistent with 10 mins). Do the skin test too! It sounds dumb, but I couldn&#x27;t imagine dumping this all over my head and then having my scalp develop an allergic reaction. That just sounds like hell to me. Alright, so I dumped it all over my head and it says to use a comb to make sure it is evenly spread out, but my hair got really knotted from all that I was doing to it so I just made sure that I soaked my hair to the very core because there was no way I was getting a comb through it.  All of the reviews say that rinsing is the most important part, but don&#x27;t freak out if your rinsing your hair and your hot water only stays on for 10 minutes. That&#x27;s what happened to me and it came out fine. Just wash it for 20 if you can or until your water gets kind of cold. As you&#x27;ll probably be able to feel, your hair gets tough because of all the rinsing so I put in conditioner and let it sit in until I had hot water again (10-20 minutes). Another side note, I&#x27;m not sure if some peoples noses are just more delicate than mine, but I do not agree with what everyone is saying about the smell. Yes, it is a little overwhelming when your applying it, but that&#x27;s because you&#x27;re using an ENTIRE bottle of it and assuming your hair is flipped over in the tub, it&#x27;s RIGHT next to your nose and eyes so it&#x27;s going to be very strong. I obviously did it in my bathroom and I had the window wide open and about 5 minutes after rinsing, I couldn&#x27;t smell it at all. My hair kind of smells like it, but  after I shower again tomorrow, I&#x27;m 100% sure the smell will be nonexistent. End results!! My hair looks almost exactly how it looked in the good ol&#x27; days before I went on pinterest and decided that ombre was for me. I will never dye my hair again, and this product is the closest thing you will get to time-traveling back in timeand slapping yourself right in the face for ever doing whatever you did to your already perfect hair color. Good luck to your hair dying adventures and remember, Hair test, skin test, be consistent, rinse, time!</li>

    <li> This works, but be sure to follow the directions EXACTLY... for example, if it tells you to RINSE your hair in the shower for 20 minutes, RINSE IT FOR 20 MINUTES.. not 18 minutes, etc.. this is a very important step, because when you are in the shower rinsing this stuff out of your hair, THATS when its really doing its job, and the cuticle of your hair is open, and THATS when all of the MOLECULES OF COLOR ( the color you hate and are trying to get rid of ) are being washed out of your hair.. so if you just give it a half hearted rinse, it may look ok for a day or two, but then, by the 3rd day, your hair will start to somewhat darken again because the cuticle has closed back up-- closed back up around those molecules of color that you hated and wanted to get rid of -- because you didnt spend enough time rinsing your hair. The usual fix would be to apply yellow-toned color if your hair turns blue, or reddish-toned color if your hair turns green (go opposite on the color wheel to tone down any given color).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The stars off are not for the fact that it didn&#x27;t remove all of my color. Take them right out of the house and dispose of them in your outdoor garbage can. These WILL NOT tone down in smell over time and if you get them on your garbage can, you&#x27;ll have to wash out your garbage can. The smell remained strong in my hair until my first COing (conditioner-only washing), then reappeared each time I wet my hair for about a month.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Burning/irritation. I definitely got burning using this product. I literally had red burns on my ears and on my neck. I don&#x27;t know if I technically have any burns on my scalp but I know that I have a burning feeling overall on my scalp.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The rinse time. Again, given that some technology went into making this product, I&#x27;m wondering why there hasn&#x27;t been some advance in how long the hair must be rinsed. Even if it&#x27;s literally impossible to accomplish such a thing, I feel a star off is in order as the rinsing time will definitely get on some people&#x27;s nerves and will use up A LOT of water, so be warned.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I don&#x27;t regret using the product. Not a pro but I&#x27;ve been doing this with myself as a guinea pig for a while.&lt;br /&gt;- LEAVE OFF YOUR JEWELRY.  This stuff turned one of my rings the same orange it turned my hair.  It&#x27;s just doing what it does.&lt;br /&gt;- Whether you went black, red or bleach blonde, your natural color has almost certainly be altered by the developer, esp with gross box dyes.&lt;br /&gt;- i.e.  You will likely have a brassy result even if your hair was once ash.  It&#x27;s worse if you&#x27;re a dark/warm/golden/red haired person though, i.e. if your hair naturally glows reddish or looks a &amp;#34;warm&amp;#34; color in the sun.  I think dying exposes that pigment and Color Oops shows that up.&lt;br /&gt;- I have never encountered any damage from this process.  Some people do though.  But most importantly DO NOT add conditioners or anything else straight after using except for a clarifying shampoo for the initial rinsing process.  I wait about 3-4 days before using any oil or conditioning products on my hair to avoid &amp;#34;trapping&amp;#34; any unwanted residual dye molecules in the hair cuticles.  So: Wash, wash, wash, THEN shampoo, then like 3 days of just combing and scraping your hair back into whatever style it agrees with.&lt;br /&gt;- I do not think it works well on stain dyes such as Manic Panic, Directions or even demi dyes, but I have successfully gotten one color out so it is worth a try if you&#x27;re desperate.  You might want to try a salon in this case.&lt;br /&gt;- Do the process in a warm room to speed it up or get the most from it.  You must RINSE well.  Otherwise the old shrunken dye molecules will bounce right back with oxidization.  Happens to me all the time with this specific color remover, which is partly why I dislike it so much compared to the others I&#x27;ve used, RE-OXIDIZATION.&lt;br /&gt;- Avoid using this process twice in a row.  If you can, wait a few days in-between if you really must, for condition AND for your poor hair&#x27;s sake.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I regret ever dying my hair or using sulfate shampoos.  If you&#x27;ve never dyed your hair and are looking into it -- at least do your research into demi dyes or think long and hard.  Maintenance, roots and damage are certainly not worth it, at least for me.  I would love to get back my pre-raphaelite hair!  Natural hair is awesome.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Tips even if they help just one person out there&lt;br /&gt;- Good professionals. (Correction, demi jobs)&lt;br /&gt;- If you&#x27;re after change, maybe try changing hair STYLE, not color.&lt;br /&gt;- Avoid permanent box dyes, or box dyes in general.  You cannot control the strength of the developer in these.  Look into getting a developer and the color to do yourself, as you can control the results much better!  (Only took me 5 years + like 30 dyes to figure this one out!)&lt;br /&gt;- If you&#x27;re impatient, slow-grower or dislike the same color, avoid henna or any super dark colors -- good luck getting rid of true BAQ henna.&lt;br /&gt;- After using every brand and product like this under the sun, I&#x27;m becoming sensitive to the nasty hair chemicals, Color Oops included. Now, rinsing my hair in very hot water for 20 minutes definitely made it dry, but in a day or two it will be back to normal.  People complain of the smell, but I didn&#x27;t think it was very over whelming at all. The smell of hair dye is way more potent. This product smelled bad, but it was a faint smell.     <li> I&#x27;ve been dying my hair for years, and anytime I&#x27;ve wanted to make a change, I&#x27;ve used Color Oops, and it&#x27;s worked! After years of dying my hair black, I used color oops and it lifted all of the black dye out, leaving the processed hair behind, which was now a lovely orangey color instead of my natural brown.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Tips:&lt;br /&gt;Don&#x27;t expect to be able to use this product and NOT dye your hair. If you&#x27;re stripping out color and leaving behing processed hair, it will have a weird tone. The chemicals don&#x27;t magically know what your original hair color is and return it.&lt;br /&gt;This product WILL NOT WORK on a non oxidative hair color like Manic Panic or other vegetable based demi-perm dyes.&lt;br /&gt;RINSE. This product works by shrinking the oxidative hair dye molecules so they can be rinsed out of your hair. If you don&#x27;t rinse well, they will reoxidize and your hair will get darker again. Also, if you don&#x27;t rinse, when you recolor your hair, those shrunken molecules will reoxidize and redeposit in your hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can recolor right away, but the color will come out several shades darker. If you wait overnight and treat with a deep conditioner the new color will be much more true.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want to get your current permenant color out, or you want to go from dyed black to blond without frying your hair, this is a great product. I was able to get all the black dye out and bleach part of my hair to almost platnium in a single day without damaging my hair.</li>

It started when my sister was going to Cosmetology school and needed a guinea pig for jobs post-graduation. It started small, with blonde and brown and red highlights. (My hair is naturally medium brown with red lights in it and also lightens a bit in the sun). Then it got bigger. I dyed my hair many times, anywhere from brown to red. Then I wanted black.&lt;br /&gt;The first time I dyed it black I let it grow out. I experimented (I was 16 at the time) with a ton of box dyes, such as auburns and dark browns, and eventually went back to jet black. I liked the jet black and thought it looked good on me (it actually paled me out, in retrospect), so I kept it until I was almost 17. Then I wanted it out, because summer was approaching. I used a hair color remover kit from the store, by myself (I think it was L&#x27;Oreal Haircolor Remover). I didn&#x27;t apply it evenly, so I ended up with bright red hair at the roots (like I was supposed to) and jet black hair from the ears down. I tried dying over it and it failed miserably. Finally, after a few weeks of this freakish hair, I called my sister.&lt;br /&gt;She chided me for using box dye, and over the next several months, we tried using Salon quality \\&quot;color correction\\&quot;. Each time we used it, my hair got even more damaged and lightened only a very little bit. Finally I let her cut off several inches of my precious long hair as she said the only way I was going to get out the black was to let it grow out. So I began the process of growing it out. Periodically over the next two years, we added some brown and red highlights to try and lighten it up. I also experimented with a semi-permanent brown dye, which I found out permanently darkened my ends. However, I finally got to the point, after a year or two, where my hair was a little multi-colored, but it was a lot more brown/red, like my natural color.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE MISTAKE:&lt;br /&gt;A few months ago, I took the nostalgia-related plunge to dye my hair dark again. Not black, but dark brown. (I know, I know, after everything I went through!). My hair was finally healthy again, since I stopped abusing it with all-over color. So, I went to my local salon and had my hair dyed (a level 3, I think). It came out darker than I expected, but I just shrugged my shoulders, knowing it would lighten up a few days after the salon. However, a couple weeks later, I saw that it was still super dark. It seriously paled me out. To boot, my hair was also damaged and breaking once again!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE DECISION:&lt;br /&gt;One night, I was laying in bed unable to fall asleep. I decided that I really wanted my hair back to its natural state. My boyfriend agreed, saying, \\&quot;As long as I&#x27;ve known you, I&#x27;ve never really seen your natural hair color.\\&quot; I got up, went on the computer, and researched my options. I only wanted to use bleach as a last resort, and I didn&#x27;t want to spend the money on the salon \\&quot;attempt\\&quot; to correct my color (since it failed so miserably in the past). I also didn&#x27;t want to contact my sister, who hadn&#x27;t known I had dyed my hair dark again, because I knew she&#x27;d berate me for making the mistake. Finally I read the reviews for both ColorZap and ColorOops. There were more good reviews for ColorOops, so at 3:30 in the morning, I headed to Walmart.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;COLOR OOPS:&lt;br /&gt;I bought two boxes because I have hair down to my breasts and it&#x27;s pretty thick. However, I only ended up using one because I felt my hair was saturated enough and wanted to minimize damage. People are right, it DOES stink like rotten eggs...but that is bearable. I also did a strand test and decided that 20 minutes would be an appropriate time to let the product sit. I found the application to be a little messy, but then again I applied it myself. I also bought a wide-toothed combto make sure it was distributed evenly, AND Aussie&#x27;s 3 Minute Miracle (always, ALWAYS my deep conditioner of choice).&lt;br /&gt;I let the product sit for twenty minutes, after I made sure it was properly rubbed into my ends. I shampooed for about 3 minutes straight and rinsed for twenty. Then shampooed again for another 3 minutes and rinsed for another 5-7 minutes (these are approximates). I got out of the shower, and even when my hair was sopping wet, I could tell it was lighter. I let it air-dry to minimize damage. I was SURPRISED!&lt;br /&gt;The color had completely drained out of my ends (a miracle considering all the abuse they took over the last few years). My hair looked like it was indeed my natural hair color, or close to it. Although, it DID turn out a little brassy, but that was OK with me. My hair didn&#x27;t feel like it was damaged much more, but I could tell some of my hair did break off. However, I do have impatience and a heavy hand with a comb.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, I am VERY pleased with this product. I feel like it removed years of hair color, even though it said it wouldn&#x27;t. I didn&#x27;t even have to use the second box, although I waited a few days before making that decision. People warned that hair darkened up after a few days...my hair didn&#x27;t seem to darken up very much at all. I didn&#x27;t dye over it, because I feel my hair color now is fabulous.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, I vow that I will never dye my hair again. Highlights are a miniscule possibility. I just want my normal, healthy hair back. I believe that, with Color Oops, I am a lot closer to achieving that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;***EDIT***&lt;br /&gt;After a week or two I did notice that my hair darkened back up a little bit, so I repeated the process with the second box of Color Oops.     <li> Most of the negative reviews I have read seem to be due to a misunderstanding of what they are getting as well as a lack of general knowledge as to how the coloring process affects your hair in general. If you dye your blonde hair darker, and then use this product,you most likely are not going to end up back you your pre dyed hair. It doesn&#x27;t work like that.Dye that uses a developer (as most dyes do)  actually lifts your hair to open the shaft for the molecules to penetrate and thus deposit color,, so it usually is not back to &amp;#34;normal&amp;#34;, just whatever the result is from the process minus the pigment..so not your natural hair, and possibly not even something that looks like your natural hair.  Don&#x27;t expect to rinse it and have a beautiful color, as this usually isn&#x27;t the case either..it is a color remover, it does not tint your hair to a more acceptable shade suited more to your tastes..that is what you do after this remover does it&#x27;s job with additional dye. It is simply removes the color.  Even with a ton of rinsing (which you HAVE to do), if you are trying to rid yourself of a dark base, it will darken slightly, as it is next to impossible to remove all color (no matter what product you use!) unless you bleach it out, which is a whole different process. As for the smell, well that is simply chemistry, it is a sulfur based, and sulfur is what actually deoxidizes the pigment, so yes, it smells bad, but is necessary, so honestly, I don&#x27;t see it as a negative as opposed to a necessary evil .It does not linger much longer then 24 hours, usually. (those of us who have used perms in the past..it is no where near as strong as that smell, thank goodness!) It is watery, but I feel like knowing this  ahead of time is winning the battle, as I really didn&#x27;t have an issue applying it to my hair at all without dripping it everywhere. Lastly, use caution when re applying dye, and try for 1-2 shades lighter than your desired shade, as well as really keeping an eye on the development, as it takes significantly less time to develop then usual. A warmer color is generally recommended, as hair treated with oops tends to pull ash, or cool..so I would really recommend a strand test before applying more color to your whole head, just in case. This is a wonderful product, but one must really be realistic and have some working knowledge of how hair coloring and processing works to prevent disappointment.velopment, as it takes significantly less time to develop then usual. A warmer color is generally recommended, as hair treated with oops tends to pull ash, or cool..so I would really recommend a strand test before applying more color to your whole head, just in case. This is a wonderful product, but one must really be realistic and have some working knowledge of how hair coloring and processing works to prevent disappointment.</li>

Her hair felt quite swollen at that point and appeared almost white.  - Applied protein rich conditioner and put her hair under the shower cap for about an hour.  - Rinsed once again and the colour had darkened slightly, to what looked like a strawberry blonde.  -Several days later...her hair looks almost as it did before she dyed it.    There is a slight strawberry tinge but no one has even noticed it. Even some of her highlights are back. The protein conditioner seemed to do the trick and her hair does not appear dry at all.     <li> I want to warn everyone that this is not a miracle treatment, especially if you have layers and layers of dark dye that you&#x27;ve built up over time.     <li> I have long thick hair (mid of shoulder blade). My original hair color is a shade of black but I&#x27;ve been lightening my color in all shades of brown for 15 years. It fills the pores and gets rid of the redness. If you do decide to dye your hair right after using the product, go with a shade lighter than intended to get the intended result. The product reaks of sulfur, but goes away several days.  Btw...there was NO damage to my hair. Apparently the product only attaches itself to the hair dye and shrinks the dye color.  This product is amazing!!!</li>

    <li> Several people have said this, but i want to emphasize it. I didn&#x27;t know enough about hair treatments to understand this at first, so excuse my ignorance, but maybe this will help another novice like me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are using oops to lighten dark hair, and if you end up with a frizzy, uneven, orange.red.yellow mess, and you want to put color back in to get to a medium color (and to smooth it out), you need to dye it twice. Here&#x27;s why. Once you have used oops, you hair will grab any dye put on it. A light brown dye will give you almost black hair. A dark blond dye will also give you almost black hair. Many people here call this \\&quot;porous.\\&quot; What I finally figured out is you can get around this problem by using a light blond dye first. Let your hair grab that. It kind-of seals your hungry hair, without turning it a dark color, so that you can then follow with a medium color like light brown or dark blond. So plan on buying oops, light ash blond, and whatever color you hope to get, preferably also in an ash shade to cut the yellow.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I still don&#x27;t understand the other options people here talk about, like protein sealers and stuff, but i guess it&#x27;s the same principle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have found the same approach works for me after a strong bleaching-stripping.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh yeah. Don&#x27;t plan to stop at the ash blond stage. My hair was still uneven and yellow after the light blond dying and definitely needed the darker color to even it out.</li>

    <li> After reading TONS of reviews on this product and a few more like it with no bleach.....  I went with two boxes of this.  I have naturally very dark hair, with a yet unknown amount of gray.  After 13 years of coloring my hair every three weeks, I decided I was going to go natural.  I talked to two different hair dressers who WOULD NOT DO IT for me!!!!  Not sure if they knew what was going to happen for sure, or just had a conflict of interest.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;BUT, this takes the color out of your hair, no doubt. But you will end up NOT your original color. Do not be deceived by other reviews, or optimistic.  Many of the warnings inside the product (not on the outside of the box mind you)  say that you will not get back your natural color, particularly if you have dark hair.  What I have learned is that even if you dye dark hair dark, as I had done to cover gray. The dark DYE actually uses peroxide to lighten your hair first and then deposits the color molecules on your hair and the developer &#x27;expands&#x27; them to stay in your hair shaft. That is how they &#x27;know&#x27; what color your hair will be when done, otherwise it would be a little different for everyone depending on your original hair color, right?  SO, if you had dark hair going into ANY other color, it will be coppery when you remove all that color. FOR SURE. (I&#x27;ll try and find the right after photos and add to this).  If you have gray or light colored hair, you will also end up with some off color, but it will depend more on what color you had colored it and I cannot speak to that...  my grays are just a lighter shade of the copper than my darks are apparently.  It will take a couple months for it to grow out and know for sure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;SO, if you are &#x27;going natural&#x27; to salt and pepper after coloring your hair dark for many years my advice to you is this.     <li> I purchased this product because I wanted to attempt to remove red permanent color from my hair. I want to note that I am not a hairdresser. Additionally, before I continue, there are a couple things to note about red dye and hair color removers in general:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Red dye has the smallest pigments and is therefore the hardest to remove.&lt;br /&gt;2. All hair color removers, no matter the brand, typically leave your hair a brassy goldish-orange color.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What you get in this kit resembles what you&#x27;d get in boxed hair dye. You&#x27;ll get an applicator bottle with developer in it and a bottle of the remover. You mix them and then apply it just like you would boxed dye. Word of warning though, it&#x27;s very watery so it will drip if you&#x27;re not careful. I applied a clear plastic shower cap while I waited just so I wouldn&#x27;t accidentally get it on any clothes or furniture. It&#x27;s not necessay but if you get it on fabric it does seem to leave a mark similar to that of a bleached spot on it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You don&#x27;t have to wait the full 20 minutes until rinsing. In fact, the instructions recommend checking on it every couple minutes to see if you&#x27;ve reached your desired results yet. I left it in the full 20 minutes. Next - rinsing. All in all you&#x27;re going to be rinsing for at least 20-30 minutes. You may think this is excessive but it&#x27;s the most important part. Don&#x27;t try to cut corners here. Additionally, make sure you get a REALLY good conditioner to use on your hair. No matter what these hair color remover boxes tell you, they are all rough on your hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I followed all the instructions. The end result? As expected it left my hair a brassy orange-blonde color. The instructions state that you can dye your hair immediately - don&#x27;t. Your hair will tend to darken for the first 24 hours or so. I consulted a couple friends who were hairdressers on how best to get back to a medium brown taking into account the brassiness. this is SO IMPORTANT - DO NOT PURCHASE A COLOR WITH ANY AMOUNT OF WARMTH IN IT. NONE. Both my friends recommended staying around a 6. So I bought a 6A which is a light ash brown. Coloring my hair was somewhat painful at this point (lots of chemicals on my scalp recently). Additionally, because of the remover it processed more quickly. My final result was a nice medium brown.
