She also ruined the shirt I was wearing by getting bleach all over it. After I deemed my hair healthy enough to redye it I decided to go back to red and just live with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My Color Oops Experience: This past weekend I decided I really wanted to go back to blonde, my hair was still pretty damaged from the salon experience and having to dye it red so often wasn&#x27;t helping anything. I found Color Oops online and began reading reviews. It seemed worth a shot (my hair was ruined, anyway) so I decided to buy some and see what happened. I also had my deep conditioner and some smoothing serum, just in case. The entire process, from the start of application to the finished product took about 2 hours. I have medium-thick hair that goes about 4 inches below the shoulders and I only used one bottle, but I had to stretch it at the end. I did a test strip for the first time in my life and determined I should leave it on for the full 20 minutes. After playing with the test strand a bit once it was dry and determining my hair was no worse for wear, I gathered up the courage to put it all over my head. After my 20 minutes were up I jumped in the shower and shampooedand rinsed my hair for the recommended 20 minutes (and was a little worried to not notice any color running out), shampooed again and rinsed for 10. My hair felt a little rough so I applied my deep conditioner all over my head twice, then did an extra time on the ends (my hair was pretty damaged from the start, so those with healthier hair probably won&#x27;t need to do that). After I was satisfied with the feel of my hair I got out of the shower, towel blotted my hair and applied the smoothing serum. I let my hair air dry overnight and when I woke up I looked in the mirror and...my hair was blonde, and it wasn&#x27;t any more damaged than before. In fact, it seemed more shiny and healthy than I&#x27;d seen it in over a year (I always apply deep conditioner and a smoothing serum after coloring my hair to try and curb the damage, but it doesn&#x27;t work as well as I&#x27;d like it to). Now, my hair isn&#x27;t COMPLETELY back to it&#x27;s natural color, it&#x27;s more of a strawberry blonde, but it&#x27;s definitely blonde, which is impressive coming from dark red. Color Oops does say if you are trying to get rid of more than one layer of color you will have to do multiple applications. You can do it right away or you can wait, as I am.  Either way, I give this product 5 stars. It removed RED from my blonde hair without noticeable damage and without breaking the bank.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My tips:&lt;br /&gt;1. Do a test strand. It will help you determine how long to leave the product on your hair and how it will handle it, as well.&lt;br /&gt;2. Wear a shirt you don&#x27;t care about if you&#x27;re as clumsy with dye as I am. It&#x27;s got a very slick consistency and I was getting droplets everywhere.&lt;br /&gt;3. Have some nice smelling hair product to put on afterward. The smell is awful, but it fades quickly after the first few hours and it&#x27;s totally worth it. If you have some product to mask the smell (as I did) use it. You won&#x27;t be able to smell your hair unless it&#x27;s up against your face.&lt;br /&gt;4. Make sure to have a back up (whether it be another box of Color Oops or some hair dye) around, just in case the color you end up with isn&#x27;t attractive. If you&#x27;re going to add color back into your hair make sure to have a protein filler, as well. Your hair will darken QUICKLY. I didn&#x27;t need either, but some people might. I recommend a second box of Color Oops, but it&#x27;s whatever feels right to you.&lt;br /&gt;5. Be patient while rinsing your hair. It takes a long time, but the more you rinse, the better your results. I was in the shower for an hour rinsing and conditioning.&lt;br /&gt;6. Have a deep conditioner ready. If you have brittle hair like me, it&#x27;s worth it. I&#x27;m not sure how healthy hair will feel, but better safe than sorry, right?commended 20 minutes (and was a little worried to not notice any color running out), shampooed again and rinsed for 10. My hair felt a little rough so I applied my deep conditioner all over my head twice, then did an extra time on the ends (my hair was pretty damaged from the start, so those with healthier hair probably won&#x27;t need to do that). I dried my hair and went to bed, not even attempting to color for 24 hours. I am happy to say that the following day I was able to achieve a light brown with one attempt and no red tints. I definitely recommend this to anyone removing red especially.</li>

We figured we&#x27;d try this because bleaching again would be more damaging) We followed the directions but when the time was up it didn&#x27;t look like it did anything.     <li> I used color oops to remove an uneven dark burgundy from my hair, and I was suprised at how well it worked.     <li> This is a detailed review because I think I have finally figured out the best way to use this, with a few additional steps that are not in the instructions. They make a very big difference. I have used this on myself and others with great results and have been coloring hair for 30 years. I really hope this helps others. These sulfur-based color removers are great but there are some things you need to know. If you are clear on what to expect from Oops and follow a few additional steps, Oops can be a lifesaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here&#x27;s a quick description of my starting hair color &amp; condition, this last time around: Long, thick, very processed hair, bleached completely in the past two months, color removed previously, bleached again, then various colors put on by a colorist at a salon, from blonde to red, all with bad results. In the end I was left with the front of my hair looking ashy green/silver and the back looking red/pink. Disaster. Horribly uneven and wrong in every way. I figured I would fix it myself and start all over. I rarely see professionals for color and I regret doing so now; I get better results on my own as long as I&#x27;m careful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Two things that make a huge difference in achieving great results with Oops (especially if you have several layers of dye on your hair, or a very dark dye): 1) a heating cap, and 2) a \\&quot;bleach wash\\&quot; at the end, also known as a \\&quot;soap cap.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For the whole process, you will need the following:&lt;br /&gt;-2 boxes of Oops (3 or 4 if you have tons of hair)&lt;br /&gt;-1 or 2 packets lightening bleach powder (from beauty supply store)&lt;br /&gt;-1 small bottle 10 volume developer (from beauty supply store)&lt;br /&gt;-clarifying (anti-residue) shampoo or dandruff shampoo&lt;br /&gt;-a small non-metallic bowl and mixing utensil (it&#x27;s essential that these not be metal)&lt;br /&gt;-a heating cap (sold on this site and some beauty supply stores)&lt;br /&gt;-several processing caps (basically just sheer shower caps like they give you in hotels)&lt;br /&gt;-re-usable latex gloves or several pairs of disposable&lt;br /&gt;-Neutral Protein Filler (beauty supply store)&lt;br /&gt;-spray bottle (optional)&lt;br /&gt;-Bragg&#x27;s apple cider vinegar (optional)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Mix up the Oops per directions. Put vaseline around your hairline because it can burn. Use the gloves they give you, and wear something that protects your upper back and shoulders. Put Oops all over your dry hair, working it in well. Then put on the processing cap (the Oops package comes with one.) Put a heating cap over this. This makes a HUGE difference to results on difficult or heavily dyed hair. It is also a great thing to have for using with deep conditioning treatments. I have the Thermal Spa Professional Conditioning Heat Cap from this site and my hair can&#x27;t live without it! It will open the cuticle shaft and allow for deeper penetration; for me, this made all the difference in results.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While you are mixing up the Oops, plug in the heat cap on High, to pre-heat. Once you have the Oops and processing/shower cap on, reduce the heating cap to level 2 (Medium) and put it on your head, over the shower cap. Wait 20 minutes. Unlike what some reviewers say, leaving the product longer will NOT help: it has a short life once it is mixed and will just stop working after 20 minutes. Then rinse like crazy. Yes, you need to rinse for 15 minutes. Set a timer in the bathroom. Do it. Shampoo with clarifying shampoo and rinse for another few minutes. Do NOT condition afterwards!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At this point, many of us need to do a second application of Oops. If your hair now looks orange (dark, medium, or light), which it almost certainly will, do a second application --- as long as you hair is not breaking off, which it should not be. Just mix up the second Oops box. No one has more processed hair than I do, and it was fine. You can do the second application on damp, towel-tried hair. Do not worry. It&#x27;s better than baking in the new color with your dryer. Put the Oops on again, with processing cap, and sit with your heat cap on one more time for 15-20 minutes. This time rinse for about 10 minutes. That will be enough. Depending on the color of your starting hair dye, result will be some shade of orange or yellow. This is normal and the best Oops or any sulfur-based remover can do. This is the whole idea, so be happy with it --- Oops will not turn your hair back to your original color. It can&#x27;t. The developers in hair dye lift molecules out of your hair so you won&#x27;t get the exact original color back. And needless to say it can&#x27;t lift out bleach if you bleached your hair previously. The idea of Oops is to either get you to a color you like enough to keep, or prepare for a new dye job by taking out old color pigment. The orange is NOT brassiness (like you can get from warm-toned hair dye), so don&#x27;t think for a second that you should put on an ash-toned color. More on that later.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is the interesting part. After doing your Oops treatment, some people say to put on a developer (10 volume) to activate any remaining color pigment after you&#x27;re done rinsing. I did that once, and sure enough, my hair got darker. Darker orange, that is. When this happens you have to keep using more color remover, which you are not going to feel like doing after all that rinsing. Believe me. After much trial and error, I&#x27;ve found the perfect final step. For me and my friends who have used it, it is brilliant. INSTEAD of using a developer, do a &#x27;bleach wash&#x27;, also known as a &#x27;soap cap.&#x27; This does the trick for me EVERY time. This last time was no exception. Here is how.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Get our your non-metallic mixing bowl and utensil. Mix up 1 oz of powder bleach lightener with two ounces 10 volume developer (20 volume if your hair is dark and not too damaged). For medium to light orange hair, or fragile hair, 10 is more than adequate. When this is mixed, add about  2-3 ounces clarifying or dandruff shampoo. Mix it all up well. Put on gloves! Massage this mixture into your DAMP hair. Add a little water and keep lathering until your hair is saturated. Throw a shower/processing cap on again but this time do NOT use heat. Check your hair every 5 minutes. Rinse out when you see a satisfactory color, or hair that is light enough that you don&#x27;t want to go lighter or cause breakage. You will be able to tell. Don&#x27;t let it sit longer than 20 minutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The bleach wash can work miracles: on me it gets rid of the ugly ashy, yellow, AND orange tones left over from both old dye molecules and the Oops. It also spares you from reactivating the color left in your hair all the time with a developer, and having to use remover over and over and over. The bleach wash gently strips and takes out the remaining dye molecules for you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I thought that the bleach wash would lighten me to the point where I could recolor, but I did not have to color over it at all. The bleach wash was all that was needed to neutralize the weird tones, and leave me with medium blonde hair with the old bleached highlights showing through nicely. No ash. No orange. Everything is even!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Note: After you rinse out your bleach wash, don&#x27;t condition just yet. You want to first check the color in the mirror to make sure you can live with it and do not plan to dye your hair right away.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;About re-coloring after Oops and a bleach wash:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want to re-dye your hair right away, do not condition just now; instead, mix 1 part Bragg&#x27;s apple cider vinegar with 2 parts water, pour over your hair, then rinse that out after a minute. This restores the hair&#x27;s PH balance, which will be seriously disrupted by the Oops. Follow the vinegar rinse with a neutral protein filler. This is essential if you plan to re-color your hair, and the Oops package even tells you so. You can buy Neutral Protein Filler online or at a beauty supply. The best way to apply the protein filler is with a spray bottle. Be generous with it. After letting the filler sit on your hair for 20 minutes, blot excess, then go ahead and color right over it. Do NOT rinse the filler out and do NOT dry your hair. Just color over it, damp and with the filler on it. However, for the love of God do a strand test with whatever color you plan to use. After all this corrective work, you don&#x27;t want to mess up. Do not use an ash-based color. It will be a disaster: dark green/purple/silver. Try a gold and go up 2 levels! If you want a level 7 blonde get a level 9 dye. If you want medium neutral blonde go with light or very light golden blonde. Just do a strand test.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you were originally blonde and you are light orange after your Oops and bleach wash, or are &#x27;almost&#x27; back to your blonde, and you think a toner will fix that and bring it to blonde, all I can say is: DON&#x27;T. Do NOT use a toner like Wella Color Charm toners that start with the letter T (T14, T10, T28 etc.). Your hair is now so porous due to the Oops and bleach wash that it will suck up the toner and turn dark dark grey or greenish/purple.  All these toners that are meant for use on bleached hair are based on blue or violet or green, and are meant to \\&quot;ash\\&quot; up the color. That&#x27;s because a normal bleach job will bring out orange/brassy tones. These are NOT the same kinds of orange/brassy tones created by color removers and a bleach wash!!! Post-bleach toners will look so dark and ugly after color remover. Trust me: I&#x27;ve done it. Then you are back to square one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are happy with the bleach wash result and will not be coloring right away, then do a Bragg&#x27;s rinse as described above, followed by a protein reconstructor (you can use the Neutral Protein Filler diluted with water: 1 part Protein Filler, 2 parts distilled water) or Joico K-Pak Reconstructor, and let that sit 15 minutes, preferably under your heating cap. Rinse that out and do a deep moisturizing mask. Don&#x27;t do an oil treatment since that requires another round of shampoo to wash out, and you want a break from shampoo right now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Don&#x27;t use more protein after this for a week. It can make fragile hair really brittle if used more often. That means avoiding hair products with Keratin or anything else that is protein.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This whole Oops/bleach wash process can take half a day but it is worth it to do it right.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I apologize to those who did not need this amount of detail.cap on again but this time do NOT use heat. Check your hair every 5 minutes. Rinse out when you see a satisfactory color, or hair that is light enough that you don&#x27;t want to go lighter or cause breakage. You will be able to tell. Don&#x27;t let it sit longer than 20 minutes.    The bleach wash can work miracles: on me it gets rid of the ugly ashy, yellow, AND orange tones left over from both old dye molecules and the Oops. It also spares you from reactivating the color left in your hair all the time with a developer, and having to use remover over and over and over. The bleach wash gently strips and takes out the remaining dye molecules for you.    I thought that the bleach wash would lighten me to the point where I could recolor, but I did not have to color over it at all. The bleach wash was all that was needed to neutralize the weird tones, and leave me with medium blonde hair with the old bleached highlights showing through nicely. No ash. No orange. Everything is even!     Note: After you rinse out your bleach wash, don&#x27;t condition just yet. You want to first check the color in the mirror to make sure you can live with it and do not plan to dye your hair right away.    About re-coloring after Oops and a bleach wash:    If you want to re-dye your hair right away, do not condition just now; instead, mix 1 part Bragg&#x27;s apple cider vinegar with 2 parts water, pour over your hair, then rinse that out after a minute. This restores the hair&#x27;s PH balance, which will be seriously disrupted by the Oops. Follow the vinegar rinse with a neutral protein filler. This is essential if you plan to re-color your hair, and the Oops package even tells you so. You can buy Neutral Protein Filler online or at a beauty supply. The best way to apply the protein filler is with a spray bottle. Be generous with it. After letting the filler sit on your hair for 20 minutes, blot excess, then go ahead and color right over it. Do NOT rinse the filler out and do NOT dry your hair. Just color overit, damp and with the filler on it. However, for the love of God do a strand test with whatever color you plan to use. After all this corrective work, you don&#x27;t want to mess up. Do not use an ash-based color. It will be a disaster: dark green/purple/silver. Try a gold and go up 2 levels! If you want a level 7 blonde get a level 9 dye. If you want medium neutral blonde go with light or very light golden blonde. Just do a strand test.    If you were originally blonde and you are light orange after your Oops and bleach wash, or are &#x27;almost&#x27; back to your blonde, and you think a toner will fix that and bring it to blonde, all I can say is: DON&#x27;T. Do NOT use a toner like Wella Color Charm toners that start with the letter T (T14, T10, T28 etc.). Your hair is now so porous due to the Oops and bleach wash that it will suck up the toner and turn dark dark grey or greenish/purple.  All these toners that are meant for use on bleached hair are based on blue or violet or green, and are meant to \\&quot;ash\\&quot; up the color. That&#x27;s because a normal bleach job will bring out orange/brassy tones. These are NOT the same kinds of orange/brassy tones created by color removers and a bleach wash!!! Post-bleach toners will look so dark and ugly after color remover. Trust me: I&#x27;ve done it. Then you are back to square one.    If you are happy with the bleach wash result and will not be coloring right away, then do a Bragg&#x27;s rinse as described above, followed by a protein reconstructor (you can use the Neutral Protein Filler diluted with water: 1 part Protein Filler, 2 parts distilled water) or Joico K-Pak Reconstructor, and let that sit 15 minutes, preferably under your heating cap. Rinse that out and do a deep moisturizing mask. Don&#x27;t do an oil treatment since that requires another round of shampoo to wash out, and you want a break from shampoo right now.     Don&#x27;t use more protein after this for a week. It can make fragile hair really brittle if used more often. That means avoiding hair products with Keratin or anything else that is protein.    This whole Oops/bleach wash process can take half a day but it is worth it to do it right.    I apologize to those who did not need this amount of detail.</li>
    <li> Didnt do SxxT. Just took out the really dark color and left the Ginger color from the brown color before it. Save your money Shave your head.</li>

    <li> This product is fantastic and well worth the 12 dollars and 40 minutes it takes from application to final rinse!  Background: I have medium brown hair and I like my natural color but sometimes I get bored and want a change.  First, my stylist colored my hair darker than it really is.  This looked great for a while -- dramatic and all -- but I got sick of it.  I wanted to go back to my natural color, but she said it would take two steps: lightening it and then dying it again (total of about 4 hours at the salon) and I started to think it wasn&#x27;t really worth how much that would cost.  Then I wondered about going red, but decided to think about it first, again because of the cost.  I ended up dying my hair myself to see if I liked red before having my stylist do it more permanently.  I used a semi-permanent medium auburn from Natural Instincts.  I liked it for two weeks and then got sick of it.  It wasn&#x27;t going to wash out for a couple of months, and I was tired of how fake it looked in the light. I beg you guys please don&#x27;t spent your money you will get better results by  just bleaching your hair. I did this process a month ago and my hair still feel dry and brittle for those of you guys that don&#x27;t know what it means to have porous hair I will leave the diffeniton on the bottom.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Porous hair is a condition of your cuticle layer. Porous hair has a raised cuticle layer that easily absorbs water and is quick to lose moisture as well.&lt;br /&gt;That what this product does it forces the cuticle layer to open because it&#x27;s taking color out and leaving it like that. This can not be fixed but you can use fillers and moisturize the hair so that it feels better.</li>
    <li> After (over) dyeing my hair black-brown (permanent) for close to four years, I was ready for a change. Preliminary research indicated I could either grow it out and cut it off OR bleach it; neither option was at all appealing to me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Somewhere, somehow, (I think it was when I was reading about bleach washing) I learned about Color Oops. I read a gazillion reviews and decided to give it a shot. It seemed like it would be far less damaging than bleaching and was much more time efficient than growing the black dye out. I picked it up at the devil&#x27;s department store, aka Wal-Mart, for just under ten dollars (my local Sally&#x27;s doesn&#x27;t carry this or any other product with hydrosulfite...I live in a rural suburb of Phoenix).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ODOR: many reviewers and YouTube videos make mention of how this product smells. Most of those who mention the smell point out the sulfur smell which is understandable since the active ingredient in Color Oops is hydrosulfite. That being said, the smell was not nearly as bad as other reviewers led me to believe. It certainly doesn&#x27;t smell GOOD, but its not the assault on the senses that I had read/heard about. I liken the smell to a milder version of a perm. I am a nursing mother and haven&#x27;t quite gotten rid of the hypersensitive nose that comes with pregnancy, so for ME to say that the smell was tolerable goes a long way. As a precaution, my husband took my daughter out of the house and when they returned about 15min after I was finished, he said there was only a mild odor lingering throughout our two-story home (I applied it in our upstairs bathroom and rinsed in the kitchen sink downstairs).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;INSTRUCTIONS: the instructions that are included are extremely clear and very detailed. If you follow the instructions, you really can&#x27;t go wrong. About the only thing I learned from YouTube and other reviews that wasn&#x27;t mentioned in the instructions was to agitate my hair as I rinsed, but I&#x27;ll get into that more below. It is important to note that Color Oops WILL NOT WORK ON VEGETABLE DYES (i.e. Manic Panic). It ONLY works on oxidative dyes. If you didn&#x27;t pour part a into part b, it isn&#x27;t an oxidative dye!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;APPLICATION: the formula of this product is VERY runny. In my situation, I needed to apply this to the ends of my hair first since they were the areas that were the most over-saturated with dye. I pulled my hair back into a ponytail and applied the solution to the pony first which made it a LOT easier to avoid spilling it all over myself and the floor. After allowing the ends to process for 10min, I saturated the rest of my hair to process for the remaining 10-15min.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PROCESSING: once I put the included cap on my head, I went outside to the warm air. The instructions are very clear to stay out of cool rooms and away from air conditioning vents/fans. Since it was a lovely 105Âº outside, I sat on the porch and let the heat help things along.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;RINSING: several other reviewers mentioned that this was the most arduous part of the process and I can&#x27;t disagree with them. While many chose to rinse the solution out in the shower (and thus running out of hot water in the process), I opted to use the kitchen sink. My faucet has a spray function and I alternated between the spray and the regular stream. I also could have used the spigot in the tub, but kneeling on the floor didn&#x27;t seem desirable at the time. This product works by opening the cuticle and breaking down the color molecules to a size that will rinse out, so keeping the cuticle open is key. The sooner the cuticle closes (i.e. by being hit with cold water), the more dye that remains in the hair. This remaining dye can and will re-oxidize over time, giving the illusion that your hair is spontaneously re-dyeing itself. To keep the cuticle open, rinse using the hottest water you can stand. Since I needed the biggest result on the ends of my hair, I was able to use water that was hotter than I would be able to useon my scalp. To \\&quot;help\\&quot; the color molecules find their way out of my hair and down the drain, I followed other recommendations to agitate my hair whilst rinsing it. I think it worked like a charm.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;RESULT: I could not be more pleased with the result I achieved. My natural color is dark brown and I feel that I was returned to that color. This product works by removing just the artificial dye molecules, and because I had been using deposit-only oxidizing color, my natural color wasn&#x27;t affected at all. See for yourself by looking at my uploaded photos.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The instructions claim that you can re-color your hair immediately after completing the Color Oops process and I would say that my hair felt like it was ready to receive color again. I didn&#x27;t have my new color on hand to re-color right away, but if I had I wouldn&#x27;t have hesitated to jump right in. I did re-color the next day after using a protein filler and my hair is really beautiful; shiny, smooth, and soft.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would absolutely use this product again in the future should I have the need and I plan to rave about it to anyone who will listen. The box states that it will only remove the most recent oxidative process that has been applied to hair, but I am here to tell you that it has removed YEARS of color from my hair. I did not have any areas that had been previously bleached (i,e, highlights) which is why I was successful in achieving my natural color. For someone who has/had highlights or who has previously bleached any portion of his or her hair, just know that it is impossible for the bleached areas to return to your natural color because the natural pigments have been removed.on my scalp. To \\&quot;help\\&quot; the color molecules find their way out of my hair and down the drain, I followed other recommendations to agitate my hair whilst rinsing it. I did not have any areas that had been previously bleached (i,e, highlights) which is why I was successful in achieving my natural color. For someone who has/had highlights or who has previously bleached any portion of his or her hair, just know that it is impossible for the bleached areas to return to your natural color because the natural pigments have been removed.</li>
